<h2 align="center">2023 OpenSSF BEST WG Meeting Notes</h2>


**[Antitrust Policy Notice](http://www.linuxfoundation.org/antitrust-policy)**

<p align="justify">Linux Foundation meetings involve participation by industry competitors, and it is the intention of the Linux Foundation to conduct all of its activities in accordance with applicable antitrust and competition laws. It is therefore extremely important that attendees adhere to meeting agendas, and be aware of, and not participate in, any activities that are prohibited under applicable US state, federal or foreign antitrust and competition laws. Examples of types of actions that are prohibited at Linux Foundation meetings and in connection with Linux Foundation activities are described in the Linux Foundation Antitrust Policy available at www.linuxfoundation.org. If you have questions about these matters, please contact your company counsel, or if you are a member of the Linux Foundation, feel free to contact Andrew Updegrove of the firm of Gesmer Updegrove LLP, which provides legal counsel to the Linux Foundation.</h2>

All OpenSSF meeting participants must comply with the OpenSSF Code of Conduct:

[Code of Conduct](https://openssf.org/community/code-of-conduct/) 

[2024 Meeting Notes](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1JY8FREBPCUUFpuv7-4B9EjeS2MLDpel0dbG5DFWrTns/edit)

<h3>**BEST WG Meeting Details**</h3>


Biweekly on Tuesdays - 10:00 AM ET/ 7:00 AM PT

[LFX Zoom](https://zoom-lfx.platform.linuxfoundation.org/meeting/97123533582?password=51bc1484-f12d-4382-b768-6d8f3c9b08c2)

[Repo](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers)  | [Discussions](https://github.com/ossf/tac/discussions)

Mailing List:  [OpenSSF](https://lists.openssf.org/g/openssf-wg-best-practices)

*Join the Mailing List to receive the calendar meeting invite**

YouTube Channel:  [OpenSSF](https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCUdhiXNEBEayowJXY_v7AXQ/) (New!)


Older 2022 notes are available [HERE](https://docs.google.com/document/d/159RLmTvW-G6DqDOw3ya-7RI5KNNd1yHxQ5XP0D9OB4o/edit#heading=h.gjdgxs)

Older 2021 notes are available [HERE](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1Fw6EIk47_rUFmi6m7jYObFofcD6gj1FK-QgGC8YuUr0/edit#heading=h.gjdgxs)

Agenda



* Welcome new friends
* Is someone willing to scribe for the meeting?
* Call for opens (list new items below)
* Open pull requests - proposal to merge. Thomas has reviewed and queued up for team review. See: [https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pulls?q=is%3Apr+is%3Aopen+label%3A%22Product%3A+Compiler+Hardening+Guide%22](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pulls?q=is%3Apr+is%3Aopen+label%3A%22Product%3A+Compiler+Hardening+Guide%22)
    * More clearly distinguish -Werror with and without selectors [https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/345](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/345) - this is a precursor for adding specific -Werror=SELECTOR values, but before we do, we need to make it clear why it’s okay to do that.
    * Discuss further how to apply the guide [https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/328](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/328)
    * Add -fno-delete-null-pointer-checks and friends [https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/323](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/323)
    * Add threat model, goals, objectives - [https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/317](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/317) - this addresses previous meetings’ discussion, which concluded that there was a need for a brief threat model
* New issues and pull requests
    * Previous meeting discussion:
        * Add -Wbidi-chars=any to counter Trojan Source attacks and threat model, goals objective ([#283](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/283), PR [#317](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/317))
            * Deals with intentionally misleading malicious code
            * Siddhesh notes this is an IDE issue
            * All agree 283 is good, 317 we feel is good content that should be broken up and inserted along with the options, but as a whole, perhaps we create a dedicated threat model (appendix, supplementary/companion doc, etc)
        * Discuss further how to apply the guide ([#328](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/328))
            * Green vs brown field projects wording
            * We will wait for David’s response and we’ll discuss in a future call
        * Add -fno-delete-null-pointer-checks and friends ([#323](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/323))
            * Have discussed this several times in the past (somewhat controversial).  Options don't make sense for using in production use cases as it could hide some bugs
            * Guide now has made distinction between release and instrumented test code, that could allow us to add these items
            * Siddhesh - perhaps add the note it could mask bugs
            * Siddhesh - the mitigation is good, but might interfere with actually finding the bugs.  This should be disabled in test
            * Thomas - perhaps move these options to their own table, removing them from he more straight-forward ones
            * 
        * Review other documents for more C/C++ compiler option ideas ([#285](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/285))
            * Listing of source materials
            * Do we import the items as issues/prs
            * Group liked the sources.  Could explore the older Wheeler doc to see what we might want to integrate as group task next year
            * 
        * Evaluate -fsanitize-minimal-runtime for possible hardening ([#326](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/326))
            * 
        * Compiler flags notes/comments by Dominik Czarnota ([#330](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/330))
            * 
        * Clarify why -O2 ([#331](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/331))
            *

Agenda



* Welcome new friends
* Is someone willing to scribe for the meeting?
* Call for opens (list new items below)
* FOSDEM’24 talk proposal submitted by Thomas
    * [https://pretalx.fosdem.org/fosdem-2024/talk/review/LLFVWUWE9UEMTK8H3FYCR98K8WVRH7GQ](https://pretalx.fosdem.org/fosdem-2024/talk/review/LLFVWUWE9UEMTK8H3FYCR98K8WVRH7GQ)
    * Talks should be selected within the next week or two
    * There will be a GCC devroom. Siddhesh offers to help broker introductions to folks there.  
* Retrospective from journey to first release of the guide:
    * What did we do well?
        * Creating focused-”for purpose” dedicated group helped the team manage themselves, maintain velocity
        * Group was able to focus on technical work quickly, which was nice; the majority of the work was on making the guide better not administration or “foundation things”
        * Having a broad contributor base of subject matter experts was great
        * Built on a lot of existing good practices,helped guide the work and consolidate the practices (pulling from these many independent sources).  Helped highlight the consensus for the desired settings
        * Able to keep up to date on latest options and keep an eye on future developments (intaking future items that have not been widely tested will be a challenge for us)
        * Having a single location for this content is VERY useful
    * What have we learned?
        * Everyone learned a lot from the contributors (thank you!!)
        * There  is no roadmap laid out by the distros on how these are set and used
        * Having diverse contributions from the technologies and distros was extremely helpful
    * What should we do differently?
        * Consider pre-briefing select media/groups for future large updates or similar projects
        * Determining how to deal with and intake future contributions - unknown today
        * 
    * What do we not understand?
        * 
* Open pull requests - proposal to merge. Thomas has reviewed and queued up for team review
    * Add -mshstk and -fsanitize=safe-stack to considered options (PR [#311](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/311))
        * Has already gotten some review/comments
        * Allows gcc to interact with shadowstack
        * Fsanitize splits the stack
        * Team agrees to merge
    * Mend fences - use 3 not 4 characters (PR [#324](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/324))
        * Minor formatting change
        * Team agrees to merge
        * There is a dependency for 325 here
    * Improve Makefile so we can more flexibly test options (PR [#325](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/325))
        * Adds printing of options
        * Team agrees to merge (after thomas fixes minor issue)
    * compiler options: simplify and clarify rpath section (PR [#327](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/327))
        * 1st time contributor went through an editing pass to make it more readable
        * Bonus note on priv escalation
        * Team agrees to merge
    * best -> good (PR [#329](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/329))
        * Based on discussion from slack
        * Toning text down from “best” to “good”
        * Team agrees to merge
* New issues and pull requests
    * Add -Wbidi-chars=any to counter Trojan Source attacks and threat model, goals objective ([#283](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/283), PR [#317](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/317))
        * Deals with intentionally misleading malicious code
        * Siddhesh notes this is an IDE issue
        * All agree 283 is good, 317 we feel is good content that should be broken up and inserted along with the options, but as a whole, perhaps we create a dedicated threat model (appendix, supplementary/companion doc, etc)
    * Discuss further how to apply the guide ([#328](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/328))
        * Green vs brown field projects wording
        * We will wait for David’s response and we’ll discuss in a future call
    * Add -fno-delete-null-pointer-checks and friends ([#323](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/323))
        * Have discussed this several times in the past (somewhat controversial).  Options don't make sense for using in production use cases as it could hide some bugs
        * Guide now has made distinction between release and instrumented test code, that could allow us to add these items
        * Siddhesh - perhaps add the note it could mask bugs
        * Siddhesh - the mitigation is good, but might interfere with actually finding the bugs.  This should be disabled in test
        * Thomas - perhaps move these options to their own table, removing them from he more straight-forward ones

Agenda



* Is someone willing to scribe for the meeting today?
* Welcome new friends
* Call for opens (list new items below)
* Next Meeting can be 19Dec (group desire to defer), No call on 2Jan2024.  1st 2024 call will 16Jan
* WG Administrivia/bookkeeping/backlog review
    * [BP Issue 220 ](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/220)- Group needs a co-lead
    * [BP Issue 255](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/255) - SOSS Taskforce - trained dev Scorecard check
    * [BP Issue 256](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/256) - SOSS Taskforce - created security trained dev job description
    * [BP Issue 257 ](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/257)- SOSS Taskforce - create security skills for devs list
    * Based on [TAC WG Lifecycle,](https://github.com/ossf/tac/blob/main/process/working-group-lifecycle.md) let’s get our PRs put together to determine which phase this WG is
* Sub-project updates (as needed)
    * C/C++ Compiler Hardening Guide live!
    * SSDGP Live!
* Review BP Roadmap to id initiatives and volunteers
* Evangelize OpenSSF “best practices” and tooling through blogs, podcasts, conference presentations, and the like. -- Create a “Secure from the (open) source” expert podcast to showcase the work across the foundation. -- As new guides/best practices are launched, we will create blogs and a conference presentation to raise awareness about it. -- Amplify talks and artifacts created by other groups within the foundation -- Create 3 EvilTux artifacts each quarter
* Create express learning classes for our body of work: working group explainer, SCM BP Guide, C/C++ Guide, Scorecard/Badges, Concise Guides
* Create a “Best Practices Member Badge” for member organizations
* Support and promote our sub-projects with contributions and feedback - Scorecard, BP Badges, OpenSSF - SkillFoundry, Classes, and Guides, Secure Software Guiding Principles (SSGP)
* Create a Memory Safety W3C-style workshop to assemble development leaders to talk about how to integrate memory safe languages and techniques more deeply into the oss ecosystem.
* Expand DEI AMA Office Hours to more broadly engage new-to-oss individuals and provide a forum for mentorship and guidance as they launch into and grow within their careers.
* Identify, curate, produce, and deliver new secure development education such as Developer Manager Training, Implementing/Integrating OSSF tools such as Scorecard, Badges, OSV, OpenVEX, etc), advanced secure development techniques, and more.
* Evangelize and embed all of our guides across OpenSSF Technical Initiatives and understand what makes sense to integrate into Scorecard
* TAC self-nominations now [open ](https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSdMkN_H3zVFW7NfZzsanF5isga3PNVUQj7-8VPlVPhb2F2iYQ/viewform)& Voter registration now [open](https://forms.gle/7suYexAnPxndvX856)

<h4>Guide Notes</h4>




* The call started with a discussion around ways of working with the guide after initial publication announcement. David suggested following the precedent set by the Concise guides, with a the text “”by the Open Source Security Foundation (OpenSSF) Best Practices Working Group, <date>” added to the top the guide (underneath title) and the date updated after new content is merged. Major milestones for the guide could still be announced in appropriate channels. It was decided to adopt the practice for now.
* The blogpost draft was reviewed by the participants. CRob agreed to be listed as co-author. After some minor editing it was decided that the blogpost can be sent to the OpenSSF TAC for review.
* Thomas announced he and Georg are planning to submit a talk proposal on the guide to FOSDEM’24. The devroom has not been decided yet. If anyone is interested to do a joint talk they should contact Thomas and Georg as soon as possible. FOSDEM submission deadline is Dec 1st, 2023. CRob offered to review the proposal before submission.
* Thomas asked about whether the participants wished the calls to continue in December or whether to have a break over the Holidays. It was decided that, assuming the release of the guide proceeds as planned, to hold a retrospective of the past year on December 6th. December 22 call will be canceled. Thomas will contact OpenSSF operations to arrange cancelation.
* Recent issues & PRs:
    * [#298](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/298) (Moved up the agenda on David’s request) - There was a brief discussion around the proposed term “instrumented test code” to refer to builds that are built with options that can detect code quality and security issues, but that are not suitable for production use. Thomas noted that “instrumented code” is a common term in academic papers when referring to code which is built with compiler-based defenses. Overall there was support for adding the proposed section. David will propose draft text in a future PR
    * [#277](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/277), PR [#276](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/276) - Thomas presented a proposal for situational options table in TL;DR list. David suggested that the table could be pivoted to allow for it to grow as new options are added ([#300](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/300)). David’s suggestion received unanimous support.
    * [#251](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/251), PR [#290](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/290) - David noted that the AdaPro C and C++ compiler is called “AdaCore GNAT Pro Enterprise” and that AdaPro GNAT may cause confusion with the upstream GCC Ada compiler. Thomas will fix the name and then merge the PR.
    * PR [#291](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/291) - Thomas noted he has updated the list of contributors before the initial release and contacted the persons added to get their consent to appear in the list. He gave them a deadline of November 29th for the acknowledgement to make it into the initial release version.
    * [#283](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/283) - David gave a summary of the “underhanded source code” threat and the possible fixes proposed in [#283](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/283). There was overall support for including the -Wbidi-chars=any but more in-depth discussion was postponed to a future call due to time constraints.

Addendum: Thomas submitted the blogpost draft and link to guide to the OpenSSF TAC mailing list later the same day and notified Jennifer Bly that the blogpost was done and submitted to the TAC for review.

<h3>Opens</h3>




* Please accept change to docs/Concise-Guide-for-Evaluating-Open-Source-Software.md proposed in [https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/246](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/246) , “Propose adding a tentative addition”. This proposes adding this point when reviewing a potential new component:
    * **What happens on a test addition?** Try adding the dependency as a test, preferably in an isolated environment, to investigate its impact:
        * 1. Does it exhibit malicious behaviour, e.g., does it attempt to exfiltrate sensitive data?
        * 2. Does it add unexpected or unnecessary indirect dependencies in production? For example, does it include production dependencies that are only required at development time or test time instead? If so, would their maintainers be willing to fix that? Every new dependency is a potential support problem or supply chain attack, so it's wise to eliminate unnecessary ones.
    * It also renumbers the following point (so it looks like it changes more than it does)
    * This was accepted per discussion below; you can see th result here: [https://best.openssf.org/Concise-Guide-for-Evaluating-Open-Source-Software](https://best.openssf.org/Concise-Guide-for-Evaluating-Open-Source-Software)
*

<h3>Meeting Notes</h3>




* 2023 summary will come in the next months… Thanks to all who participated in SCM and Compiler guide and ongoing interest.  If anyone has ideas for other initiatives, we will continue toi provide updates to those but if you have other ideas we can set up small groups.
* **Compiler guide** [Thomas Nyman]: FYI update - working hard on getting initial version into a shape where we’re proud to publish it. Not intended to be a finished product but you can consider it a MVP. We’ve been preparing a blog post. Current plan we aim to post it Nov 29. Still working on sign-off on text. It might slip but hope is to get it out by end of nov - and some mention in upcoming OpenSSF day Japan…  \
Link to draft here: [https://docs.google.com/document/d/1pqxOBxhH95XcbY-dNj1e8BMrH9bSgFIsQvgP7E7oz1c/edit](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1pqxOBxhH95XcbY-dNj1e8BMrH9bSgFIsQvgP7E7oz1c/edit) 
* Best practices badge picked a new logo - that will be updated in the coming weeks - a new blog on “evil tux” to be posted about the badge. Scope for coordinating neytwe
* Educational material - David has been collecting info and coming up with proposal… will share soon.
* Dan: suggest a deliverable possibling coming out of the [Secure the Web Forward](https://www.w3.org/2023/03/secure-the-web-forward/) workshop - something addressing needs of web developers
* Seth: Python guide similar to NPM guide
* Avishay: memory safety SIG - we want to provide memory safety recommendations for languages that are memory safe but could be made unsafe… Could we do that under memory safety SIG?
    * Crob - probably best and then we get the word out…  Every time we talk to US gov they are interested in memory safety - EU commission have similar concerns….
    * Thomas: I also think that’s great.
* Seth: Rust guide … would be good.
* David: between linux kernel and curl we have lots of experience of re-writing portions of things in Rust. Linux kernel is adding support for device drivers in rust - device drivers is the thing they’re most worried about. Interesting side effect: Rust really “likes” certain kind of calls and not others, and the kinds it likes are less likely to produce vulnerabilities. They’ve modified parts of the Linux kernel in C to be friendlier to Rust callers. The unexpected effect of the changes is to reduce the likelihood of certain problems, sometimes helpful. Also changing their use of C … to reduce certain kinds of defects.
* Crob: tools: new guides; blogs; conferences; 
* Seth: lowering the bar - you don’t have to “rewrite” it in Rust - middle ground - could be easier to achieve if you have concrete examples & stories.
* **PR 246**: update the concise guides… [https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/246](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/246) [see above] - All agreed to it, it was merged during the meeting. Note: The change looks larger than it is, it renumbers “9” to “10” which caused many trivial changes

* Marketing request has been submitted. Regarding the timing, Jennifer Bly mentioned she would prefer to spread out the marketing announcements in time, i.e., if we want to publish a blogpost, it would be best not to do that right on top of OpenSSF Day Japan (Dec 4th). Instead, at the day itself, it would be mentioned that the release of the guide has happened. To accommodate this, Georg suggested aiming for Nov 14th, which is quite soon. Thomas has reached out to CRob for WG lead approval. There should also be time for review by the TAC.
* Long discussion about timing. We’ve been trying for an aggressive deadline - is this too aggressive?
* We are taking two more weeks for further improvements and discussing the open PRs listed below. The new target date is the last week of November.
* We are planning to inform the TAC about the final version on the meeting of November 22
* We collected plenty of high-quality feedback from across the OpenSSF and external experts, therefore we won't open for another round of feedback
* There are a number of outstanding PRs, need to try to work/merge them
* Recent issues & PRs:
    * Compiler Hardening Guide should include -fcf-protection ([#247](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/247), PR [#260](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/260))  - _David flagged this as important to address before initial release_
        * #260 is good to go in, even if it extends the TL;DR section
    * Add -mshstk to the C/C++ Compiler Hardening Guide? ([#267](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/267))
    * Options -Wtrampolines and -fstack-clash-protection not universal ([#277](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/277))
    * fix -fPIC -shared taking precedence (PR [#276](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/276)) 
    * Compiler Hardening Guide should refer to more compilers based on GCC and clang ([#251](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/251))
    * Continue review of issue [97](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/97) and early OpenSSF [guide](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1SslnJuqbFUyTFnhzkhC_Q3PPGZ1zrG89COrS6LV6pz4/edit)

* Recent issues & PRs:
    * Add note in table 1 about -Werror ([#149](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/149), PR [#253](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/253)) - _David flagged this as important to address before initial release_ - remove -Werror from TLDR, change paragraph on it 1 sentence, move details to lower section
    * Add note about system includes to hardening guide (PR [#259](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/259)) - related to above
    * Add -Wimplicit-fallthrough (PR [#262](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/262)) - _David flagged this as important to address before initial release_
        * Add citation: https://eel.is/c++draft/dcl.attr.fallthrough
    * When compiling compilers, make their defaults secure (PR [#261](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/261)) - _David flagged this as important to address before initial release_
        * Thomas will try to move into its own section
        * Performance issues matter
        * We don’t need all the details, just point out the importance and list examples (1 GCC, one clang)
    * Add -fstrict-flex-arrays. Fixes [#249](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/249) (PR [#263](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/263/)) - _David flagged this as important to address before initial release_
        * We’ll add discussion about the other levels, but encourage the use of level 3
        * Some use levels 0…2 because they’re using old compilers that don’t support C99 (e.g., vim)
        * Thomas will propose text to explain levels 0..2
        * Levels documented in the -Wstrict-flex-arrays section in the gcc man page
    * Add branch protection flags (PR [#260](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/260)) - _David flagged this as important to address before initial release_

* Any other concerns/formalities regarding release?
* Pull Requests:

    * #259: Approved in principle.  To be merged before next meeting.
    * #262: C++’s description of [[fallthrough]]: https://eel.is/c++draft/dcl.attr.fallthrough

        Resolution: Accepted in principle. To be merged before next meeting.

* #261: David suggests to record the issue, but no pressing need to have it resolved before release 1.0.  Needs more iterations.
* #263: Encourage use of 3 as default.  Accepted in principle.

    * We closed issue 102 [Issues · ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers (github.com)](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/102)
    * Taking a look at #155 [Add Azure DevOps to SCM Best Practices · Issue #155 · ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers (github.com)](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/155) we think while we want to incorporate other SCM platforms the relative priority of Azure is probably low compared to some others?  Also - we need people who can provide that info - and the expertise; also it’s not open, it’s for private… So maybe we should close this?
    * #153 [generic language vs contextual guidance · Issue #153 · ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers (github.com)](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/153) - lots of language and guidance specific to particular personas… a lot of things not applicable to all personas who might be reading this doc…
        * How to account for this without inordinate complexity… 
        * Some of comments are general comments - 
        * For personas we could map it to the personas documented in the personas work (e.g. written by the toolbelt effort). [toolbelt/personas at main · ossf/toolbelt (github.com)](https://github.com/ossf/toolbelt/tree/main/personas)
        * Agreed we don’t want multiple documents - multiple pages one for each personas - we need to keep it simple.
        * “Be permissive of when a particular recommendation would apply…”
        * Could be an indent under each item…
        * Also there’s some duplication…
* Next steps
    * Probably to replay above on the next BP call and schedule a working session to go through ideas in #153.

    * Continuing discussion on guidance for GCC's -fstack-protector on Aarch64 ([#234](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/234), PR[ #235](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/235)) - Thomas has updated PR[ #235](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/235) based on discussion on [2023-09-27](#bookmark=id.863n4hp4nw9q).
        * Siddhest and David commented on the wording on GitHub

    * Reopened by David: Discussion on -Wall and production code vs. production of code in ([#149](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/149))

        * -ftrivial-auto-var-init ([#245](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/245)) - 
            * Siddhesh noted the performance regression reported by systemd developers should be noted in the description

            * Siddhesh noted that there are other architecture-specific flags that should be considered

            * Siddhesh noted that -fstrict-flex-arrays is now used in Linux kernel.

    * Jared Miller (SAP)
    * Dana Wang (LF)
* Call for opens (list new items below)
* WG Administrivia/bookkeeping/backlog review
* Sub-project updates (as needed)
* Review, discuss, and adopt/reject MVSR:

**Mission**

Our Mission is to provide open source developers with security best practices recommendations and easy ways to learn and apply them.  We seek to fortify the open-source ecosystem by championing and embedding best security practices, thereby creating a digital environment where both developers and users can trust and rely on open-source solutions without hesitation.

**Vision**

We envision a world where software developers can easily IDENTIFY good practices, requirements and tools that help them create and maintain secure world-class software, helping foster a community where security knowledge is shared and amplified.  We seek to provide means to LEARN techniques of writing and identifying secure software using methods best suited to learners of all types. We desire to provide tools to help developers ADOPT these good practices seamlessly into their daily work.

**Strategy**

To achieve our Mission and Vision, the BEST Working group will execute on the following strategy:



1. Collaborate with security experts to draft a comprehensive set of best practices tailored for open-source projects.
2. Identify gaps in tools and resources that provide opportunities to promote and implement secure development practices.
3. Evangelize and drive adoption of our artifacts (ex: guides, trainings, tools) through community outreach and targeted maintainer engagement.
4. Collaborate with other OpenSSF and open source efforts to provide comprehensive guidance, advice, and tooling for software developers and open source software consumers to use, implement, and evaluate the security qualities of software.

**Roadmap**

To deliver on our Strategy, the BEST Working Group will do the following:



* Evangelize OpenSSF “best practices” and tooling through blogs, podcasts, conference presentations, and the like.
    * Create a “Secure from the (open) source” expert podcast to showcase the work across the foundation.
    * As new guides/best practices are launched, we will create blogs and a conference presentation to raise awareness about it.
    * Amplify talks and artifacts created by other groups within the foundation
    * Create 3 EvilTux artifacts each quarter
* Create express learning classes for our body of work: working group explainer, SCM BP Guide, C/C++ Guide, Scorecard/Badges, Concise Guides
* Create a “Best Practices Member Badge” for member organizations
* Support and promote our sub-projects with contributions and feedback - Scorecard, BP Badges, OpenSSF - SkillFoundry, Classes, and Guides, Secure Software Guiding Principles (SSGP)
* Create a Memory Safety W3C-style workshop to assemble development leaders to talk about how to integrate memory safe languages and techniques more deeply into the oss ecosystem.
* Expand DEI AMA Office Hours to more broadly engage new-to-oss individuals and provide a forum for mentorship and guidance as they launch into and grow within their careers.
* Identify, curate, produce, and deliver new secure development education such as Developer Manager Training, Implementing/Integrating OSSF tools such as Scorecard, Badges, OSV, OpenVEX, etc), advanced secure development techniques, and more.
* On Roadmap above, do we want to commit to taking all of our guides and seeing what makes sense to integrate into Scorecard?

Agenda



* Welcome new friends
* Is someone willing to scribe for the meeting?
* Call for opens (list new items below)
* When to announce the RFC for the compiler options guide on the OpenSSF mailing list?
    * Among those present there were no objections for announcing RFC on mailing list. Thomas will prepare the announcement.
* Recent issues:
    * [CVE-2023-40339](https://nvd.nist.gov/vuln/detail/CVE-2023-40339) affecting GCC's -fstack-protector on Aarch64 ([#234](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/234), PR[ #235](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/235)) - active discussion in the issue on whether addressing specific vulnerabilities is appropriate for the guide.  \
How should the guide address vulnerabilities in recommended options?

Is recommending the latest compiler versions sufficient?

* Siddhesh noted that most compiler hardening features can be affected by heuristics which may not give consistent results in all configuration. Listing ALL caveats which may adversely affect coverage may require too much effort from a guide maintenance point of view and detract from the main goal of the document: listing good practices. Addressing the broader concern may require a separate project.
* Given the specific concerns, it can be argued that the issue affecting GCC may not be a vulnerability at all and the assignment of the CVE may be “jumping the gun” (related recent talk by Siddhesh: [https://siddhesh.in/files/Security-Processes.pdf](https://siddhesh.in/files/Security-Processes.pdf))
* William Huhn commented that from a practitioner point-of-view, the issue is something that really should be cleared about. The CVE system is important in getting people to take action.
* One approach to address the issue would be to direct to use the latest branch from GCC 7 onwards should be ok + general guidance on not using unsupported compiler versions 
* Gabriel noted that intent of the document should not be to jump on every CVE, but in this particular case the severity  wide applicability justifies discussion and describing the issue. The CVE number helps in disambiguating the issue, and may be justified to refer.
* Siddhart commented that it might be useful to also include sample code that illustrates the issue.
* Thomas will make attempt at rewording current PR to “tone down” CVE aspect, but addressing how deployers of stack-protector can get better results going forward by using appropriate versions of GCC.    
    * Compiler Hardening Guide should recommend -fhardened ([#240](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/240)) 
-fhardened is an umbrella option that in the current proposal enables:
        * -D_FORTIFY_SOURCE=3 (or =2 for older glibcs)
        * -D_GLIBCXX_ASSERTIONS
        * [-ftrivial-auto-var-init=zero](https://gcc.gnu.org/pipermail/gcc-patches/2021-February/565514.html) (not currently covered by guide)
        * -fPIE  -pie  -Wl,-z,relro,-z,now
        * -fstack-protector-strong
        * -fstack-clash-protection
        * -fcf-protection=full (x86 only, not currently covered by guide)

            Siddhesh noted the flag is under discussion and is currently targeting GCC 14. Another caveat is that the specific flags enabled by -fhardened may shift from version to version in GCC. Unclear how to address that in the guider. 


            Gabriel suggested keeping the issue open until the option is available in an official GCC release (expected in May 2024).


            William Huhn noted he likes the flag but was worried whether the sub-options enabled -fhardened have been vetted for performance. Siddhesh noted that the features proposed to be included by -fhardened are standard options used by Linux distributions. He also noted the proposal excluded options that may have been controversial (but these decisions may change in future releases)


            Siddhesh noted that -ftrivial-auto-ver-init=zero has [potential performance issues](https://gcc.gnu.org/bugzilla/show_bug.cgi?id=111523). There’s also -fstrict-flex-arrays.


            It was decided to keep the issue open until -fhardened is available in an official GCC release but work on the additions to the guide can proceed in the meanwhile as the discussion around the functionality stabilizes in the GCC community.   

    * Missing Binutils version for -rpath and --enable-new-dtags ([#164](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/164), PR [#233](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/233))
        * Merged after brief discussion.

The rest of the items on the agenda were postponed for the next call.



* Reopened by David: Discussion on -Wall and production code vs. production of code in ([#149](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/149)) 
* Continue review of issue [97](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/97) and early OpenSSF [guide](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1SslnJuqbFUyTFnhzkhC_Q3PPGZ1zrG89COrS6LV6pz4/edit)

Agenda



* CRob is on vacation this week!
    * David A. Wheeler will facilitate
* Is someone willing to scribe for the meeting today?
* Welcome new friends
* Call for opens (list new items below)
* WG Administrivia/bookkeeping/backlog review
* Sub-project updates (as needed)
* Memory Safety SIG update (Avishey):
    * Memory Safety Project Support Program:  [https://docs.google.com/document/d/1IYSVyOdXK7cvep0shr33tXvUlSTmCllG6LJHiNfVrWM/edit#heading=h.p7dcxo3ha8e1](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1IYSVyOdXK7cvep0shr33tXvUlSTmCllG6LJHiNfVrWM/edit#heading=h.p7dcxo3ha8e1) 
        * Please review & comment!!
    * David: Funding: That has to be approved by someone with funding authority. Small amounts might be possible via sos.dev, but larger amounts need to be approved by GB or from existing accounts. Alpha-Omega is funding Rustls (via Prossimo) and Rust in the Linux kernel.
    * David A. Wheeler: US government is very interested in memory-safe languages.
* What about OpenSSF AI/ML WG
    * David: AI/ML tools’ code generation is amazing, but they’re trained on insecure code, so they tend to generate insecure code, as shown by experiments.
    * Victor Lu created this document:  [https://docs.google.com/document/d/1veEdcQAqf2KhXTf7YlOW_lIif8kCDNgLGRqLqi70F44/edit](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1veEdcQAqf2KhXTf7YlOW_lIif8kCDNgLGRqLqi70F44/edit)
    * OpenSSF AI/ML WG collaborates with AI & Data Foundation, which is GREAT, because we need collaboration of the security experts & the AI/ML experts
    * OpenSSF AI/ML Working Group Meeting Notes: [https://docs.google.com/document/d/1hEJdr7yXv5tfYpUfn_e7DAUTyvoU6mY0b9eH6EXAHaI/edit](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1hEJdr7yXv5tfYpUfn_e7DAUTyvoU6mY0b9eH6EXAHaI/edit)
    * Might be useful to remind AI/ML that you also need to use the capabilities of “normal” code
    * AI & Data Foundation is short-staffed
    * David A. Wheeler: My graduate course includes material on AI & Security: :[https://dwheeler.com/secure-class/presentations/Secure-Software-10-Misc.ppt](https://dwheeler.com/secure-class/presentations/Secure-Software-10-Misc.ppt)
* What about ONCD RFI
    * OpenSSF is working on a response in a committee

<h4>Guide Notes</h4>




* Chris: I will work on something for github/gitlab… - github and gitlab icons - people don’t know they can be clicked on - and they’re terrible for accessibility.
* Dan: totally agree -
* Christine: PR to re-organize some of the repositories sections… mix of configurations vs. best practices (e.g. update repo frequently - not really a configuration).
* … also use of the word _should_.
* Christine: another feedback we got from people working with lots of repositories - how can you add these things at scale. Rulesets in GitHub - related to branch protection - but should be more at the top level.
* Dan: suggest Operations / Specific Recommendations - and making it a small item.
* Regulatory
    * Dan: looking for feedback on how SCM guide fits together with regulations - David Wheeler’s view is that the regulation 
    * Aeva: some NIST guidelines are relevant to SCM… Yes it could be valuable in a guide to map things to regulatory requirements - but be careful on wording that it would fulfill - maybe “might fulfill” or “similar” – or connecting and saying “here are the frameworks you should know about.”
    * Christine: could this be level up?
    * Aeva:
  [M-22-18 (whitehouse.gov)](https://www.whitehouse.gov/wp-content/uploads/2022/09/M-22-18.pdf); 
  [NIST Special Publication 800-series General Information | NIST](https://www.nist.gov/itl/publications-0/nist-special-publication-800-series-general-information)
    * Aeva: advise high level guidance…
* Blog post to go out 14-Sep: [https://docs.google.com/document/d/1PaXZOd7dnGZMmhvqnvvsQ2WxhimlzClwvCq1jqsv29s/edit](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1PaXZOd7dnGZMmhvqnvvsQ2WxhimlzClwvCq1jqsv29s/edit) 
* Christine to do a talk at OpenSSF day…
* _we take a look at Chris’s proposal_
    * First option that Chris presents just adds text links for github and gitlab - 
* Chris: suggest a table…
* Dan: suggest a table for next steps… after the current announcement.
* Chris: also tables not easy to manipulate when they get large…  - although table would look neater…
* **We agree to go with option 1- adding text links for github and gitlab and adding “Applies to:” for items that don’t have singleton pages**
* **We agree to skip next call as it’ll be Open Source Summit EU…**

Agenda



* Welcome new friends
* Is someone willing to scribe for the meeting?
* Call for opens (list new items below)
* Status on preparation for first release
    * More cleanup has been done
    * Update of README still as todo
* Review proposed pull requests:
    * Move -D_LIBCPP_ASSERT to list of considered options ([#225](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/225)) - to be replaced with libc++ “hardened mode”
* Review existing issue [97](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/97) and early OpenSSF [guide](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1SslnJuqbFUyTFnhzkhC_Q3PPGZ1zrG89COrS6LV6pz4/edit) 
    * -Wl,--hash-style=gnu option in guide draft may have been added as alternative to _DT_HASH_ in 2006 which at least have been slow, although it is unclear whether this has had any security implication [https://sourceware.org/pipermail/libc-alpha/2022-August/141304.html](https://sourceware.org/pipermail/libc-alpha/2022-August/141304.html)
    * -Wl,--no-copy-dt-needed-entries and -Wl,--as-needed affect symbol resolution in a way that allows symbols defined in dynamic libraries to be later replaced, similar to LD_PRELOAD, but using a more obscure mechanism [https://github.com/elfmaster/dt_infect](https://github.com/elfmaster/dt_infect). This has a security implication, but the description needs to be amended to more clearly explain this
    * `-fexceptions `can be security-relevant for multi-threaded applications as without unwind tables there is a higher risk of deadlock 
    * The implications -fasynchronous-unwind-tables is unclear, although it might be related to the unwind table implementation in compilers. Gabriel offered to follow-up with Florian Weimer who made the original suggestion to the incubation guide.
    * -fplugin=annobin seems to be specific to Red Hat, maybe should be covered in considered options table
    * `-grecord-gcc-switches` may be relevant from a QA-perspective since it can allow determining which (hardening) flags were used, although it may not always be practical for production code. Could be included in a debug-build specific table. 
* Next steps
    * Georg raised the question whether we should target announcing the RFC for the compiler guide either before the OSSummit in Bilbao on Sep 19-20, 2023 or after. It was agreed to put this on the agenda for the next meeting.

<h4>Opens</h4>




* Feedback from sharing SCM guide with the Best Practices community (aggregated [here](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1HZtCu6okqTaISY_ugljeXhNndMXWm3G14KknR9xZ6SM/edit))
    * [Chris] It’s not obvious that the GitHub and GitLab icons are clickable links, and that they lead to explanations. Plus the links are not accessible.
        * **Chris**: to send a **PR addressing accessibility**, ex: using text links 
    * [Christine] Managing repos at scale is hard to do with the guidelines.
        * [Chris] Suggest having language that recommends setting organization-wide policies.
        * [Christine] For handling repos at scale could invite the community to contribute scripts, etc. via discussions
    * [Chris] Some of the recommendations are a mix of configurations and other “best practices” ex: repository updates.
        * **Christine**: Send a PR **organizing the Repository section** recommendations to see if it reads better
    * Scorecard above 7 feedback says they don’t want to be penalized for a low score. 
        * [Chris] These are recommendations and should not be seen as penalizing. The guide does have language of these being recommendations.
    * Would like to see the guide formulated more as a list of possibilities than a list of things you "should" do.
        * **Christine: request suggestion on what language would work better**.
* GitHub rulesets feedback from Legitify. Not looking to put it in their tooling and suggest having these in the SCM guide
    * We could put it in the GitHub top-level README
        * **Christine**: send a PR **adding rulesets**
    * We don’t have GitLab expertise in this project. Hopefully the community can jump in and contribute post-launch.
    * [Chris] Suggest putting a call-to-action in various channels
    * [Christine] Can to a CTA at TODO group meetings and at OSS EU in September

<h3>Meeting Notes</h3>




* OSSF Day in Spain ([https://events.linuxfoundation.org/openssf-day-europe/](https://events.linuxfoundation.org/openssf-day-europe/))
* Secure Software Guiding Principles (SSGP)
* Guidance that SW devs will consider when developing both open source and proprietary SW (public pledge)
* Take to OSSF TAC for vote adoption
* Benefits
    * Accessible to customers
    * Easy to read English
    * Industry reputation
    * Alignment within a company
    * Competitive advantage
    * Support safe harbor claims
* [https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/212/files](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/212/files) 
    * Hasan - Could something be added about architecture as sometimes this falls short as well?
    * David - Add a phrase along the lines of “will learn” the common vulnerabilities and how to mitigate them. I.e. top CWEs ([https://cwe.mitre.org/top25/](https://cwe.mitre.org/top25/)) 
    * David - What about smaller developers contributing in their free time?
        * Initially, the goal was large companies
        * Would like feedback from individuals
    * Lots of +1s, no spoken/chat objections
    * Are there any other standards?
        * IBM Secure Engineering Framework - compatible with NIST standards
        * [https://www.redbooks.ibm.com/abstracts/redp4641.html](https://www.redbooks.ibm.com/abstracts/redp4641.html)
        * [https://www.ibm.com/support/pages/ibm-security-and-privacy-design](https://www.ibm.com/support/pages/ibm-security-and-privacy-design)
        * [https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-218.pdf](https://nvlpubs.nist.gov/nistpubs/SpecialPublications/NIST.SP.800-218.pdf) 
        * [https://csrc.nist.gov/Projects/ssdf](https://csrc.nist.gov/Projects/ssdf)
    * <span style="text-decoration:underline;">( ) Merge</span> this in as a draft to get more formal feedback. Timeline - wrapped up in the next 3 weeks (**September 1st, 2023**)
    * <span style="text-decoration:underline;">( ) CRob</span> to setup a few working sessions to work on this in real time
* GitHub discussions
    * How can we leverage this? Is this useful?
    * Categories could be helpful
    * Only have history in Slack for 90 days
        * CRob suggest posting important discussions here instead of Slack so history isn’t lost
    * Examples:
        * [https://github.com/todogroup/ospology/discussions](https://github.com/todogroup/ospology/discussions)
        * [https://maintainers.github.com/](https://maintainers.github.com/)
    * David - thinks issues should go in issues, i.e. where should content go?
        * Christine - agrees could have info scattered across the digital universe
    * Chris - GitHub used to have discussions at Team levels and this went away and is now open. So visibility matches repos visibility - most likely not an issue for this group
    * Currently organized by repo for OSSF
    * Thomas - sees potential to cover discussions that are tabled from meetings and would be easier/more visible than OSSF meeting notes
    * Hasan - get notes as close as possible to the code level so think of the notes as code in order to track versions of notes
    * Should we put together usage guidelines?
        * Yes
        * Christine interested in helping
        * Turn this into a BKM (Best Known Method) to share with other groups
* [BP Issue 207](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/207) (Adoption of Sterling Toolchain/Security Toolbelt SIG)
    * Chris - only comment to sway in one group versus another but maybe put this in the Security Tooling group versus this group but unsure of actual metric how this would impact contributions
    * CRob has a conflict with the Tooling group
* Who would like to assist in crafting an MVSR for the BEST WG - [BP Issue 214](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/214)
    * Mission Vision Strategy and Roadmap
    * States the how
    * CRob needs help in creating the MVSR for this group - most of it is predefined in the readme and ( ) CRob will transfer this into the MVSR format
    * Christine, Hasan will help contribute
    * 80% Draft before the summit
    * How is this visible to the sub-groups? Do they need to contribute as well?
        * If they are producing SW then they would need at least roadmap whereas this is more of a high-level objective
    * High level goal of a MVSR for all groups but also see how they could contribute and tie together. 2 hour Zoom meeting in a couple weeks
    * One goal would be further reach of devs to share this work
* We’re moving bestpractices.coreinfrastructure.org -> [www.bestpractices.dev](http://www.bestpractices.dev) - staging works, plan to do this to the “real site” soon.
    * Will redirect for a while but please switch over

<h3>Opens</h3>




* (Seth) Intent to create a set of packaging best practices for Python developers. Likely some overlap with best practices of many ecosystems (VCS like GitHub, GitLab)
* Jeffrey borek: vis-a-vis the license…  a recent blog post about licencing recently - and relevancy of license, see: [https://www.infoworld.com/article/3703768/the-licensing-war-is-over.html](https://www.infoworld.com/article/3703768/the-licensing-war-is-over.html)
    * David: Many cans of worms - the best practices badge and scorecard says “hey is there a license” & require is. From a BP badge - my focus is more on security & sustainability. If you want something to be secure over time it needs to be sustained - in order for it to be sustained it needs to have a license. So even if you don’t care about legal risk (and you should), licenses matter for sustainment (since people are less likely to contribute to unlicensed software), and sustainment is important for long-term security. Risk. “Developers care about” - yes most developers don’t know about the law, but software engineering people often don’t learn these… a lot of developers are unaware that there are laws in the world that apply to their business. Many developers don’t know what the law requires, but that lack of knowledge doesn’t matter, laws are still important.
    * Dan: I would discount this view. Speaking as someone at a company who works with engineers that do care about licenses - and with a legal team that does care about licenses. And as someone who does have opinions about licenses… [https://www.torgo.com/blog/2023/06/whats-the-deal-with-open-source-open-data-and-open-standards-licenses.html](https://www.torgo.com/blog/2023/06/whats-the-deal-with-open-source-open-data-and-open-standards-licenses.html) 
* Seth: Python best practices … touches on source control management…  Proposing some new work…
    * Crob: I support… 
    * Similar to NPM BP Guide - [https://github.com/ossf/package-manager-best-practices/blob/main/published/npm.md](https://github.com/ossf/package-manager-best-practices/blob/main/published/npm.md) 
* Sarah: Joined to find out what the state of discussion of secure software guiding principles.
    * Will find…

<h4>OpenSSF Best Practices Badge project (David A. Wheeler)</h4>




* Working to move best practices badge to bestpractices.dev (may end up being [www.bestpractices.dev](www.bestpractices.dev)).
* In principle this should be easy, but when originally developed this wasn’t the plan, & some documentation is pretty bad, so we’re finding various problems along the way.
* Put notes in “Moving best practices badge to bestpractices.dev” [https://docs.google.com/document/d/1xn8U_Sp770cmp-W6qPYLy_3b0S1TozEU6Ft6UBihwy8/edit](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1xn8U_Sp770cmp-W6qPYLy_3b0S1TozEU6Ft6UBihwy8/edit) 
* If anyone has experience in such moves, happy to talk offline.
* Goal is to make “everything just work” - using Fastly CDN  so a little more complicated.

Agenda



* Welcome new friends
    * Andres Orbe - Alpha Omega
* Is someone willing to scribe for the meeting?
* Call for opens (list new items below)
* Review proposed pull requests on guide:
* Mark options with performance impact in recommended options table ([#144](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/144))

Thomas has added a general remark that some options may have a performance impact and providing additional details regarding performance implications in the detailed description of the options.


There is some concern that by just mentioning performance impact, some targeted adopters of these compiler options will opt to not enabling them. \
Might be useful to be up-front about performance concerns to mitigate the chances of looking a bit shady.


We may recommend to perform proper benchmarking if performance is critically important.


Solution: write a paragraph about benchmarking. Note speed, binary (stored) size, runtime memory use. 
 
Proposed paragraph:


“Many of the compiler options detailed below may have an affect on the software's performance. Engineers should evaluate any trades-offs of enabling more secure options versus observed performance test data within the context of their software's use cases. Prior to making any changes in production environments, thorough testing should be conducted to understand how the compiler hardening options affect the performance and security aspects of the software. Remember that a system that works quickly, but for an adversary, is typically not what a user wants.”

* Flag usage recommendations, order sensitivity ([#165](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/165/))

Thomas has added text outlining that distributions may use different default options.


David recommends to add a neutral statement that some options may be order-sensitive. Typically, the option provided last takes precedence over the same options provided earlier


Generalize whenever possible (GCC and clang). However, “clang -v” doesn’t do this. Also note Microsoft’s compiler.


Also add, earlier, “Note that some flags are order-sensitive; in particular, if you set the same parameter more than once, the later one typically governs all parameters after that point.”. See also: \
gcc -O2 -dM -E - < /dev/null

* Add list of considered but excluded options ([#184](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/184))
    * Everyone loved this!
    * David W: Add this sentence just before the last intro sentence (“The following table…”): “While they are not in the recommended list, you may find them useful for your purposes.”
* David W: you can see a “pretty” version of the draft here: [https://best.openssf.org/Compiler-Hardening-Guides/Compiler-Options-Hardening-Guide-for-C-and-C++](https://best.openssf.org/Compiler-Hardening-Guides/Compiler-Options-Hardening-Guide-for-C-and-C++) This is using the “Simplest Possible Process” for publication which the best practices WG is experimenting with.
*

**Discussion on Outreach / Education**


Jeffrey: Discussion of AI & security…

**SBOM-a-rama highlights** … quick summary is - a lot of work ongoing to turn the idea of SBOMs into reality. And making big changes industry-wide is hard. There are folks doing it right now. But lots still in progress.


Crob: a role we could help with is - making it easy for upstream maintainers to work it into their workflow. We can provide tools, education for  developers, then we go out and raise awareness. That’s our tactic with OpenVEX. Get upstream to start producing VEX so people across the supply chain can start deciding how to take action. We had the idea of a **podcast** that went into the education plan. Podcast dedicated to OSS security … supply chain security… someone could come talk about each of our topics…

    * Would like to rename directory “Compiler_Hardening_Guides” to change underscores to dashes per [https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/163](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/163)

    * [https://bp.openssf.org/Compiler_Hardening_Guides/Compiler-Options-Hardening-Guide-for-C-and-C++.html](https://bp.openssf.org/Compiler_Hardening_Guides/Compiler-Options-Hardening-Guide-for-C-and-C++.html)
* Topics related to QA & co-operation around the guide:
    * On issue [#149](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/149) it was pointed out in the last meeting that the issue highlights the more broader topic of how do we ensure the quality of the guide? Should principally accept contributions as long as they fit the scope and format of the guide or should we strive to validate each submission, e.g., against reference code? (what should that be?)
    * We’re generally happy with what we have so far
    * Proposed changes need to be reviewed, accepted by general consensus, take a vote if that’s what’s needed to determine consensus.
    * If an option is more specific, perhaps put that in separate table to identify “specialized” options & explain in what cases it would be useful.
    * Our scope includes code for IoT (device makers).
    * David has created a push request
* Recently opened issues:
    * Should we be recommending options that aren't very portable? (Issue [#146](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/146), [#148](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/148))
    * Recently opened issues:
* Perhaps move some “test only” flags to their own section (so they’re not lost), e.g., assertions. We don’t want test-only flags in the production list of flags!

    * Home on OpenSSF, click through to GitHub
    * Is that the desired end state?
    * Follow the pattern from Concise Guides etc…
    * _discussion on the final product for this and other items like it - maybe using Jekyll to publish a prettier format on openssf.org website…_
    * Amanda: can use a github page…  Need to work on Branding in CSS.
    * David: one quirkiness is generated files should be in some directory that represents the repo…  As long as the URL is stable then it’s fine.

* DevRel issues: [https://github.com/ossf/tac/issues/169](https://github.com/ossf/tac/issues/169)
    * Is there interest from this group?
    * Christine: Yes!
    * David: YES!
        * There are many good ideas here. A quick win would be creating the Dedicated "Landing Page" Specifically Aimed At Maintainers.
    * Dan: YES. And hopefully can get our dev rel team involved as well.
    * David: creating a dedicated landing page <- a good idea
    * Crob: in diagrammers society - we’ve discussed a persona view. Help walk these people through what they want to do…
    * Arnaud: I agree – she is telling us we’re failing in one of our main goals - we’re not making ourselves relevant. Communication geared towards member companies. So we need to take this seriously. She was nice enough to come up with suggestions,. We need to take this into account.
    * Dan: support - love the idea of a slack channel or something - this needs to be staffed up. We could use the existing slack as a way to engage maintainers.
    * Crob: we are hiring a community manager. [https://jobs.smartrecruiters.com/LinuxFoundation/743999909659433-community-manager-openssf](https://jobs.smartrecruiters.com/LinuxFoundation/743999909659433-community-manager-openssf)
    * This and the previous point have interrelationship - better publishing… We don’t have to wait for the hiring to do the landing page… 
    * Crob:  since we do interact with maintainers more than other groups - i spent some time working with a project - found how they executed their project landing pages. Impressive resources available. Videos, etc.. encouraging new contributions and community contribution. How can we do the same? Any suggestions?
    * Arnaud: we shouldn’t expect maintainers to join our cause … if they hear about us can they quickly find information that is usable to them… That’s the model we should have. Landing page is low hanging fruit. **Get to the OpenSSF web site and quickly find the page that gives them actionable information. **
    * Crob: we’re not looking to deputize .. but in vancouver we had developers start bp badge app process during the presentation. We need to make it simple. Maintainers want to do the right thing.
    * Christine: good way for member companies to get feedback .. we can bring it back into BP guide…
    * CRob: We at Intel are trying to integrate hundreds of projects with Scorecard.
        * David: As a quickstart, we could add those repo URLs into the list of a million projects we score weekly. It’s better to integrate “current commit” process, but that can happen incrementally.
        * Maybe that could be mentioned in the “developer landing page” (is that what we’re calling it?)
    * Randall: I want to help. 
    * 100s of projects integrated with scorecard - cheat code - scorecard folks already do analysis of xxx projects… It would still be good for repos to implement the action.
* David: I’d like to briefly return back to the “making nicer looking pages”. Here’s one proposal:
    * This WG already maintains the main results in a “docs/” subdirectory.
    * Proposal: experiment with using GitHub’s built-in mechanisms (Jekyll, etc.) to generate a tree of static HTML + CSS, and link to it via “bp.openssf.org”. That can be done quickly & I have experience doing that, we can then see if that’s what we’d like to do. The resulting pages would be served from “[https://bp.openssf.org/PATH](https://bp.openssf.org/PATH)” (giving us stable URLs) & other openssf.org pages can link to that.
    * Christine: support
    * Amanda: I support
    * _some discussion on how to do the CSS_
        * I would recommend if using the CSS from the wordpress site, that CSS should be version controlled, if not already, and both sites always use the same version so they stay in sync
        * David: CSS can include other CSS. Probably the best way to do this is to have a “main” CSS that the other CSS files include.
    * David: I’ll give this a try.
    * Arnaud: Be careful, Jekyll can become complex.
    * David: I agree! If you just modify basic configuration settings, select templates, and modify CSS, you’re fine. If you start modifying code that can be a deep problem. GitHub can run arbitrary workflows, but if we can avoid complex workflows that’d be better
* Perhaps it’d be good to mock up a landing page.
    * David: How about “docs/developers.md” as “landing page for developers”. We can mock up a first draft.
* Dan Appelquist: Scorecard4Purl <- new tool! (dan). Takes a package URL (pURL) as a parameter, uses GitHub & Scorecard API to produce information on that pURL.
    * [https://github.com/torgo/Scorecard4Purl](https://github.com/torgo/Scorecard4Purl) 
    * Awesome!
    * Scorecard -\-ECOSYSTEM_NAME package can do something similar (adding NuGet) - willing to add a “-\-purl PURL” option?
    * Laurant/Azeem in Scorecard team is interested in improvements, contact them via Slack
    * [https://github.com/ossf/scorecard#using-a-package-manager](https://github.com/ossf/scorecard#using-a-package-manager)
    * It’s not a command line tool, but there’s some similar information available at [https://deps.dev/](https://deps.dev/) & metrics.openssf.org

Agenda



* Feedback that we’ve received - discussing feedback from end users’ group
    * Feedback from the … group … folks love the best practices guides but sometimes don’t like them – concerned with drift.
    * They have some policy applied and someone reverts – they don’t have a way to check …
    * Noam: this is what legitify solves… run the tool in a periodic manner.
    * Interested in the framing around why it’s important and enforcing those policies - advice for tooling. Mentioned some gaps that might exist in github…
    * Notes from Slack on TODO Group (Open Source Program Office feedback)
        * Some recommendations that target corporate-controlled organizations (member SSO) may not be appropriate for community projects
        * The guide would be more useful if it was framed around how the policy could be maintained. Without enforcement, policies can get stale, so recommendations around tooling, ex: safe-settings is important. The gap here is that SCMs don't provide out-of-the-box features for policy as code to help with this.
        * OpenSSF should drive collaboration to share use cases and scenarios. This would be the next step after best practices guides which is where similar efforts begin (as an example, license compliance efforts have moved beyond guides to examples).
        * Different orgs might have different security set-ups… a case study - 
            * main area vs. labs area
        * Having more examples… use cases and scenarios… 
            * When license compliance was kicking off a lot of best practices shared… now people sharing data… sharing opinionated data…  Use cases, case studies…
            * In the roadmap for the future.. 
            * GitHub Discussions… ?
            * Case studies as well….
    * From End User wg - good feedback…
        * Relationship with SLSA
        * Noam: these documents - a framework - this document checks many of the requirements for the source code part. E..g they require code review; they require SSO for users; etc… many points that we meet.
        * Christine: in Vancouver I spoke about how it’s related to SLSA…
        * Also some feedback
    * Avishay : presented at MS and got questions about scalability of some of the rules - 
        * Difference between orgs with many open source maintainers / etc…
            * E.g. not allowing people to create public repos… hard to scale some projects without allowing those.
            * 
    * Dan: maybe make it clearer that legitify …   add to the frontmatter of the document… as well as scorecard… running audits periodically  
        * Need for tools…
        * SCMs don’t provide out of the box…
* We need to make it more clear that these are best practices and some of them might not apply … 
    * Tag enterprise policies as only applicable to “closed source” orgs…
    * Add “**how should people read the document**” material… to take a stab.
    * Maybe some material on “how to take your private stuff public” 
        * Christine: yes also 
    * This doc is broader than the open source community…
* Links in the docs
* Thoughts on things that could be added to the doc:
    * Tooling Part
        * **Noam to take a stab at the tooling.**
    * Going Public - moving from private to public
        * Sometimes repos get transferred…
        * **Christine to see if she can make a PR**
    * How to read this document
        * **Dan to do a PR on how to read this document**
    * More in-depth case studies… (maybe not ready for that yet)
    * Start a community / how to contribute (discussions) - can raise on the next best practices call. Dan to propose of GitHub Discussions.
    * What should be the stable URL for the SCM guide
        * **Dan to bring up at BP Call** <- use something like github pages?
    * New issue: [Add Azure DevOps to SCM Best Practices · Issue #155 · ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers (github.com)](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/155)
        * How to address?
        * Should it be added to legitify?
        * Noam: for now we can add it to markdown… keep same structure… if policies added to the document earlier we will add it internally…
        * Chris: What are the acceptance criteria for SCM services?
        * Dan: feels like we should have rough consensus of this group and the Best Practices group… 
            * Avishay: also impact on open source supply chain. OSSF intention is to increase the level of security in open source software… One metric could be “does it allow for open source projects”?
            * Chris: tooling should be friendly to open source projects…
        * Noam: I think we should freeze addition of SCMs and get to “1.0” before we add new SCMs.
            * _general agreement_
            * Christine: we need criteria for future roadmap…

* Is someone willing to scribe for the meeting today?

* Note: CRob is on PTO today
* Call for opens (list new items below)
* WG Administrivia/bookkeeping/backlog review
* Sub-project updates (as needed)
* [Jonathan] The Great Repository Audit, which is proposed effort outside this group.
* Proposed SIG under “Securing repositories” WG, may be funded by Alpha-Omega.
* Major artifact servers (PyPI, Maven Central, RubyGems, etc.) often haven’t had pen tests. Often pen tests are performed when someone acquires your organization, but since they’re provided for free, there’s been no economic pressure to perform a pen test on them. “We may be running before we walk”.
* Note: Premise isn’t always right, many projects _do_ have pen tests performed on them. But these projects aren’t necessarily evaluated from a security POV, if they haven’t then let’s do it.
* Frankly, most proprietary software & services also haven’t undergone a pen test, security audit, or similar. It’s something that doesn’t happen often. So let’s address this.
* A SIG meeting has been added, every Thursday 9am ET (unless securing repo WG is ongoing).
* Idea: OpenSSF funds pen tests of major artifact servers.
* [https://openssf.slack.com/files/U01LYFRTSQ7/F0595TSF2TA/the_great_artifact_repository_audit](https://openssf.slack.com/files/U01LYFRTSQ7/F0595TSF2TA/the_great_artifact_repository_audit)
* [https://docs.google.com/document/d/1EzYfM5-S5I27fC8_YE-bN-nm-J8Q1tG6aC_MKYpUvH0/edit#](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1EzYfM5-S5I27fC8_YE-bN-nm-J8Q1tG6aC_MKYpUvH0/edit#)
* [Amanda] Consolidating info into a “single repo of truth” [https://github.com/ossf/community](https://github.com/ossf/community)
* Jonathan: Vulnerabilities Disclosures WG has proposed an OpenSSF “outbound vulnerability policy” with a model outbound vulnerability disclosure policy. TAC ratified.
    * [https://docs.google.com/document/d/1W2Xfw9i5pSA-0XbIw3a4kcW2o4PByxDbjcnWe9mlQwA/edit#](https://docs.google.com/document/d/1W2Xfw9i5pSA-0XbIw3a4kcW2o4PByxDbjcnWe9mlQwA/edit#)
* It needs to be posted on OpenSSF website & foundation repo

* Thomas suggested spending some time on discussing ways of working: whether we should tag stable releases
    * Randall suggested tagging specific versions in the Github repository
    * Georg noted that having some sort of releases allows writing blog posts to make both developers and compiler community aware of the guide and can also reported towards the TAC 
    * Siddhesh suggested loosely tieing stable guideline releases to compiler releases to the compiler release cadence, e.g., having releases December / June would allow time to incorporate changes after GCC / LLVM releases.
    * We have a few big “feature” packages, e.g. merging old guide from Google Doc, the contributions from Microsoft and Intel which would make sense to finalize before an initial “big” release.
* Avishay asked whether the initial submissions from Microsoft should be as complete as the initial contribution from Ericsson or whether it can proceed more iteratively. 
    * No opposition to proceeding iteratively and bringing changes up for discussion in the bi-weekly calls as content becomes available for review.
* Thomas will make a suggestion on guidance for citation style that can be discussed in a future meeting.
    * Siddhart referred to [https://fedoraproject.org/wiki/Security_Features_Matrix](https://fedoraproject.org/wiki/Security_Features_Matrix) as a suggestion for how to structure information.
* On issues [#146](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/146) and [#148](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/148):

    * Gabriel noted we want to be more precise when attributing options to any tool, including linker.
    * Siddhesh volunteered to improve the references to specific linker versions and possibly add a note on the deprecation on gold deprecation
* On issue [#149](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/issues/149) Gabriel pointed that the issue highlights the more broader topic of how do we ensure the quality of the guide? Should principally accept contributions as long as they fit the scope and format of the guide or should we strive to validate each submission, e.g., against reference code? (what should that be?)   
    * It was agreed to continue this discussion in the next meeting.

<h4>Opens</h4>




* 

<h4>Guide Notes</h4>




* Thomas tried to address the feedback to [#132](https://github.com/ossf/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/132) in [ran-dall/wg-best-practices-os-developers #1](https://github.com/ran-dall/wg-best-practices-os-developers/pull/1). Discussion on this to continue offline.
* Gabriel presented the Microsoft SDL C++ hardening guide which offers broader advice on C++ software security
    * In terms of compiler flags, the guide recommends C++ Core Guideline’s Support Library (GSL) and static checkers in favor specifying compiler hardening options explicitly but there the guide covers compiler features, such as stack corruption prevention, code flow integrity such as shadow stack etc.
    * Also recommends specific C++ data types, e.g., secure versions std::vector and std::string - Covers only C++, advice on C development outside of scope
    * David likes the idea of a separate document for guidelines for the Microsoft compiler. Trying to merge the clang+gcc material AND the Microsoft material into a single table wouldn’t make sense, as the syntax and meanings of the options are very different. He’s also wondering whether compiler-independent guidance of libraries should be independent, as that is common to C++ development regardless of compiler.
    * Overall consensus seems to be to have a separate section and table for the Microsoft compiler, where specific options can be linked to the equivalent options in GCC and Clang. That will make it easy for users who just want to see the options to enable for the various compilers, _and_ simply the ability to cross-link when that’s sensible. Gabriel and Michael will come back with a proposal.
* Continuing discussion on -fno-delete-null-pointer-checks. 
    * The option will require the compiler to generate the null-check, but a null-pointer dereference can potentially be seen by the optimizer before -> a deference can still occur, but the option can reduce the impact of vulnerabilities. However, the specific contexts where the option is important are potentially narrow, e.g., OS kernel development, or during testing for null pointer conditions.
        * David disagreed: ALL programs, kernel and application, have the potential to have null dereferences when the language permits them. It’s not even limited to C/C++. He joked, “the primary purpose of a Java compiler is to generate code that raises null dereference exceptions.” It’s not an application vs. kernel difference, it’s something else.
    * The ensuing discussion seemed to suggest there would be a need to address the importance of specific functions from an _operational point of view_, and the _point of view of debug and fuzz testing_.
        * In operations, you want to minimize the risks (likelihood & impact) of vulnerabilities. So you want to minimize the impact of an error. When doing traditional functional _testing_ you want the software to be as similar as possible as the software that will be used in operations, so in functional testing you want to use the operational parameters.
        * When doing debugging & fuzz testing, you want to _maximize_ the chance that a mistake reveals itself (e.g., crash when anything isn’t right), to increase the likelihood of detection of vulnerabilities/problems before shipping. In these cases you do _not_ want the software to hide problems, but instead maximize the probability of detection.
    * Specific types of testing, e.g., fuzzing, can have further considerations, e.g. during fuzzing you want to ensure dangerous behavior is triggered on as often as possible, and consequently want to avoid options which potentially hide specific unsafe conditions.
    * From the point of view of the guide, we should also consider the priority of different options for the reader, i.e., make it clear which options are most important to avoid overwhelming the reader with a large number of options to implement and test.
    * Based on the discussion, Thomas will make a proposal to restructure the current “Recommended Options” to separate tables focused on operations vs. fuzz testing needs specifically.
* Next meeting overlaps Open Source Summit. Perhaps should cancel & re-meet in 4 weeks.
